Images of HSC J091843.27-022007.5 show a red galaxy with two blue point sources at either side, separated by 2.26 arcsec. This system has a source and a lens redshifts z<SUB>s</SUB> = 0.804 and z<SUB>\u2113</SUB> = 0.459, respectively, as obtained by our follow-up spectroscopic data. CXCO J100201.50+020330.0 shows two point sources separated by 0.85 arcsec on either side of an early-type galaxy. The follow-up spectroscopic data confirm the fainter quasar has the same redshift with the brighter quasar from the Sloan Digital Sky Survey (SDSS) fiber spectrum at z<SUB>s</SUB> = 2.016. The deflecting foreground galaxy is a typical early-type galaxy at a redshift of z<SUB>\u2113</SUB> = 0.439. SDSS J135944.21+012809.8 has two point sources with quasar spectra at the same redshift z<SUB>s</SUB> = 1.096, separated by 1.05 arcsec, and fits to the HSC images confirm the presence of a galaxy between these. These discoveries demonstrate the power of the Hyper Suprime-Cam Subaru Strategic Program (HSC-SSP)'s deep imaging and wide sky coverage. Combined with existing X-ray source catalogues and follow-up spectroscopy, the HSC-SSP provides us unique opportunities to find multiple-image quasars lensed by a foreground galaxy.", "doi": "10.1093/mnras/stab145", "custom1": "eprint: arXiv:2006.16584", "issn": "0035-8711", "number": "1"}, "ADS link": "https://ui.adsabs.harvard.edu/abs/2021MNRAS.502.1487J", "Publisher link via ADS gateway": "https://ui.adsabs.harvard.edu/link_gateway/2021MNRAS.502.1487J/PUB_HTML", "Action": "Scanned and processed all tables", "Paper text": "\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n<!DOCTYPE html>\r\n<html lang=\"en\" class=\"no-js\">\r\n\r\n<head>\r\n                        <title>Survey of Gravitationally Lensed Objects in HSC Imaging (SuGOHI) \u2013 VII. widget-instance-OUP_Article_FullText_Widget\">\n        <div class=\"module-widget\">\r\n    <div class=\"widget-items\" data-widgetname=\"ArticleFulltext\">\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n                    <h2 scrollto-destination=227346033 id=\"227346033\" class=\"abstract-title js-splitscreen-abstract-title\" >ABSTRACT</h2>\r\n<section class=\"abstract\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">We present spectroscopic confirmation of three new two-image gravitationally lensed quasars, compiled from existing strong lens and X-ray catalogues. Images of HSC J091843.27\u2013022007.5 show a red galaxy with two blue point sources at either side, separated by 2.26 arcsec. This system has a source and a lens redshifts <em>z</em><sub>s</sub>\u00a0= 0.804 and <em>z</em><sub>\u2113</sub>\u00a0= 0.459, respectively, as obtained by our follow-up spectroscopic data. CXCO J100201.50+020330.0 shows two point sources separated by 0.85 arcsec on either side of an early-type galaxy. The follow-up spectroscopic data confirm the fainter quasar has the same redshift with the brighter quasar from the Sloan Digital Sky Survey (SDSS) fiber spectrum at <em>z</em><sub>s</sub>\u00a0= 2.016. The deflecting foreground galaxy is a typical early-type galaxy at a redshift of <em>z</em><sub>\u2113</sub>\u00a0= 0.439. SDSS J135944.21+012809.8 has two point sources with quasar spectra at the same redshift <em>z</em><sub>s</sub>\u00a0= 1.096, separated by 1.05 arcsec, and fits to the HSC images confirm the presence of a galaxy between these. These discoveries demonstrate the power of the Hyper Suprime-Cam Subaru Strategic Program (HSC-SSP)\u2019s deep imaging and wide sky coverage. Combined with existing X-ray source catalogues and follow-up spectroscopy, the HSC-SSP provides us unique opportunities to find multiple-image quasars lensed by a foreground galaxy.</p></section>                    <div class=\"article-metadata-panel clearfix at-ArticleMetadata\"></div>\r\n<div class=\"kwd-group\"><a class=\"kwd-part kwd-main\" href=\"javascript:;\" data-keyword=\"&quot;gravitational lensing: strong&quot;\">gravitational lensing: strong</a>, <a class=\"kwd-part kwd-main\" href=\"javascript:;\" data-keyword=\"&quot;methods: observational&quot;\">methods: observational</a></div>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=227346035 id=\"227346035\" class=\"section-title js-splitscreen-section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec1>1 INTRODUCTION</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">Over the four decades since the discovery of the first gravitationally lensed quasar (Walsh, Carswell &amp; Weymann <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib62\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib62\" data-open=\"bib62\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">1979</a>), these systems have proven to be invaluable probes for both astrophysics and cosmology (e.g. Claeskens &amp; Surdej <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib10\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib10\" data-open=\"bib10\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2002</a>; Treu &amp; Marshall <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib59\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib59\" data-open=\"bib59\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2016</a>). Astrophysical applications range from intermediate redshifts, with the measurement of extragalactic extinction curves (e.g. Falco et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib16\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib16\" data-open=\"bib16\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">1999</a>; \u00d8stman, Goobar &amp; M\u00f6rtsell <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib67\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib67\" data-open=\"bib67\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2008</a>), the direct detection of dark matter substructures (e.g. Dalal &amp; Kochanek <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib11\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib11\" data-open=\"bib11\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2002</a>; Vegetti et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib60\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib60\" data-open=\"bib60\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2012</a>), constraints on Warm Dark Matter (WDM; e.g. Inoue et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib23\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib23\" data-open=\"bib23\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>), microlensing studies Vernardos &amp; Tsagkatakis (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib61\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib61\" data-open=\"bib61\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2019</a>), and the calibration of the stellar mass Fundamental Plane (e.g. Schechter et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib48\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib48\" data-open=\"bib48\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2014</a>), to high redshifts, with elucidating the structure of quasar accretion discs (e.g. Yonehara et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib65\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib65\" data-open=\"bib65\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">1998</a>; Poindexter, Morgan &amp; Kochanek <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib46\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib46\" data-open=\"bib46\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2008</a>), their broad line regions (e.g. Sluse et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib52\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib52\" data-open=\"bib52\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2012</a>; Fian et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib17\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib17\" data-open=\"bib17\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2018</a>), and the coevolution of supermassive black holes with their hosts galaxies (e.g. Peng et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib45\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib45\" data-open=\"bib45\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2006</a>; Ding et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib13\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib13\" data-open=\"bib13\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>). In cosmology, statistically complete samples of lensed quasars are used to set constraints on dark energy (e.g. Oguri et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib41\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib41\" data-open=\"bib41\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2008</a>, <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib42\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib42\" data-open=\"bib42\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2012</a>), and lensed quasars with measured time delays are used to infer the Hubble\u2013Lema\u00eetre constant independent from other probes (e.g. Suyu et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib57\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib57\" data-open=\"bib57\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2010</a>; Bonvin et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib7\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib7\" data-open=\"bib7\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>; Wong et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib64\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib64\" data-open=\"bib64\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2019</a>).</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">While these applications are broad, they all require distinct sample selection criteria, such that studies utilizing lensed quasars are limited at present by the small number of \u223c220 known systems.<sup><span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fn1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fn1\" data-open=\"fn1\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-fn js-xref-fn\">1</a></sup> None the less, the numbers have increased considerably over the past decade and a half, due to the availability of large-scale, deep multiband optical imaging surveys such as the Sloan Digital Sky Survey (SDSS; York et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib66\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib66\" data-open=\"bib66\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2000</a>), and more recently the Panoramic Survey Telescope and Rapid Response System (Pan-STARRS; Chambers et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib8\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib8\" data-open=\"bib8\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2016</a>), the Dark Energy Survey (DES; Abbott et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib1\" data-open=\"bib1\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2018</a>), the Hyper Suprime-Cam Subaru Strategic Program (HSC-SSP; Aihara et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib3\" data-open=\"bib3\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2018a</a>), and the Dark Energy Spectroscopic Instrument (DESI) Legacy Imaging Surveys (Dey et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib12\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib12\" data-open=\"bib12\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2019</a>). Various data mining techniques have been employed to isolate the intrinsically rare lensed quasars (Oguri &amp; Marshall <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib39\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib39\" data-open=\"bib39\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2010</a>) among the vast amounts of possible contaminants. These include selecting from a parent spectroscopic catalogue and applying morphological and colour criteria (e.g. Oguri et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib40\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib40\" data-open=\"bib40\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2006</a>), using machine learning techniques on both catalogue and pixel data (e.g. Agnello et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib2\" data-open=\"bib2\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>), or engaging citizen science volunteers to visually inspect large numbers of images (e.g. Sonnenfeld et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib55\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib55\" data-open=\"bib55\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2020</a>). Ultimately however, to convincingly confirm a system as a lensed quasar requires extensive follow-up spectroscopy campaigns, which is why publishing lists of candidates is common in the literature (e.g. Rusu et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib47\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib47\" data-open=\"bib47\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2019</a>; Chan et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib9\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib9\" data-open=\"bib9\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2020</a>).</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">In this paper, we present the spectroscopic confirmation of three new strongly lensed quasars compiled from previous catalogues applied to the HSC-SSP footprint: HSC J091843.27\u2013022007.5, CXCO J100201.50+020330.0, and SDSS J135944.21+012809.8 (hereafter J0918, J1002, and J1359) at (RA, Dec.) = (139.6803, \u22122.3354), (150.5063, +2.0582), and (209.9342, +1.4693), respectively. Our paper is organized as follows. Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec2\"></span><a href=\"#sec2\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec js-xref-sec\">2</a> briefly illustrates the candidate-compilation process. In Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec3\"></span><a href=\"#sec3\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec js-xref-sec\">3</a>, we describe the imaging analysis. We present the results of the spectroscopic follow-up observations of the systems in Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec4\"></span><a href=\"#sec4\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec js-xref-sec\">4</a>. In Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec5\"></span><a href=\"#sec5\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec js-xref-sec\">5</a>, we present the mass modelling of the systems, and we conclude in Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec6\"></span><a href=\"#sec6\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec js-xref-sec\">6</a>. Throughout this paper, we adopt a concordance cosmology with \u03a9<sub>m</sub>\u00a0= 0.27, \u03a9<sub>\u039b</sub>\u00a0= 0.73, <em>H</em><sub>0</sub>\u00a0= 73\u00a0km s<sup>\u22121</sup> Mpc<sup>\u22121</sup>. All quoted magnitudes are on the AB system, position angles are measured East of North, and uncertainties are 1\u03c3 and are assumed to be Gaussian.</p>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=227346039 id=\"227346039\" class=\"section-title js-splitscreen-section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec2>2 LENSED QUASAR CANDIDATE COMPILATION</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">The lens candidates we report here are not the result of a single systematic search. Instead, we compiled candidates from three different methods employed by several of the authors: looking for close companion object in the Chandra catalogue of X-ray selected objects (Evans et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib15\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib15\" data-open=\"bib15\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2010</a>), carried out by co-author Anupreeta More, re-inspection of the Sloan Digital Sky Survey Quasar Lens Search (SQLS; e.g. Oguri et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib40\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib40\" data-open=\"bib40\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2006</a>; Inada et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib22\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib22\" data-open=\"bib22\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2012</a>) catalogue, conducted by co-author Issha Kayo, and further examination of the Survey of Gravitationally lensed Objects in HSC Imaging (SuGOHI; Sonnenfeld et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib53\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib53\" data-open=\"bib53\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2018</a>, <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib54\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib54\" data-open=\"bib54\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2019</a>, <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib55\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib55\" data-open=\"bib55\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2020</a>; Wong et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib63\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib63\" data-open=\"bib63\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2018</a>; Chan et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib9\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib9\" data-open=\"bib9\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2020</a>; Jaelani et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib26\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib26\" data-open=\"bib26\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2020</a>).</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">As preliminary selection, we checked 5 candidates of SQLS on HSC footprint to see whether we can clearly observe an extended object (galaxy) between two point sources with quite similar colours. J1359 was the only promising candidate for spectroscopic follow-up. We selected 3 of 15 candidates from the SuGOHI lenses (e.g. Chan et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib9\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib9\" data-open=\"bib9\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2020</a>; Jaelani et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib26\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib26\" data-open=\"bib26\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2020</a>; Sonnenfeld et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib55\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib55\" data-open=\"bib55\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2020</a>) based on their brightness and with suitable coordinates for follow-up.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">In total, we selected 5 candidates, two from the first two methods each, and three from SuGOHI, for conducting follow-up spectroscopic observations. Details of each candidate are described in the next sections.</p>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=227346043 id=\"227346043\" class=\"section-title js-splitscreen-section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec3>3 IMAGING</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">In this work, we use photometric data from the HSC Wide S18A internal data release of the HSC survey (Aihara et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib5\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib5\" data-open=\"bib5\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2019</a>). The HSC Survey is an ongoing imaging survey, expected to cover about 1400\u00a0deg<sup>2</sup> in five bands (<em>g, r, i, z</em>, and <em>y</em>) down to <em>r</em>\u00a0\u223c 26 with the Hyper Suprime-Cam (Aihara et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib3\" data-open=\"bib3\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2018a</a>; Furusawa et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib19\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib19\" data-open=\"bib19\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2018</a>; Kawanomoto et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib29\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib29\" data-open=\"bib29\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2018</a>; Komiyama et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib32\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib32\" data-open=\"bib32\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2018</a>; Miyazaki et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib36\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib36\" data-open=\"bib36\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2018</a>), using a wide-field (1.7-deg diameter) optical camera installed on the 8.2-m Subaru Telescope. The data are processed with <span class=\"small-caps\">hscpipe</span>, which is derived from the Vera C. Rubin Observatory\u2019s Legacy Survey of Space and Time pipeline (Ivezi\u0107 et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib25\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib25\" data-open=\"bib25\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2008</a>, <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib24\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib24\" data-open=\"bib24\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2019</a>; Axelrod et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib6\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib6\" data-open=\"bib6\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2010</a>; Juri\u0107 et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib27\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib27\" data-open=\"bib27\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>).</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">We model and analyse the multiband HSC imaging data for the lens systems using <span class=\"small-caps\">galfit</span> (Peng et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib44\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib44\" data-open=\"bib44\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2002</a>). For each system, we measure relative positions of the fainter quasar and the lens galaxy with respect to the brighter quasar, by fitting a model composed of a point source for each quasar image and a S\u00e9rsic profile convolved with the point spread function (PSF) for the lens galaxy. The PSF models are generated using the <span class=\"monospace\">PSF Picker</span> tool Aihara et\u00a0al. (see details in <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib4\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib4\" data-open=\"bib4\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2018b</a>, <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib5\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib5\" data-open=\"bib5\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2019</a>) for all of the HSC bands. Magnitudes of each component, derived from the fits, are given in Table\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-tbl1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"tbl1\" data-open=\"tbl1\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">1</a>.</p>                    <a id=\"227346046\" scrollto-destination=\"227346046\"></a>\r\n<div content-id=\"tbl1\" class=\"table-modal table-full-width-wrap\"><div class=\"table-wrap table-wide\"><div class=\"table-wrap-title\" id=\"tbl1\" data-id=\"tbl1\"><span class=\"label\">Table 1.</span><div class=\"caption\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">Properties of three confirmed lensed quasars. The redshifts of lens and source are obtained from our follow-up spectra. The relative astrometry in <em>i</em> band in arcsec, and the magnitudes of the brighter (A), the fainter (B) quasar image, and the lens galaxy (G) are obtained by fitting the HSC images using <span class=\"small-caps\">galfit</span>. The HSC image quality, in terms of the \u2018seeing\u2019 FWHM in arcsec, is also quoted. A tentative result <em>z</em><sub>\u2113</sub>\u00a0= 0.35 for J1359.</p></div> </div><div class=\"table-overflow\"><table role=\"table\"><thead><tr><th>System [<em>z</em><sub>\u2113</sub>,        </a></div></div></div><p class=\"chapter-para\">In Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" data-modal-source-id=\"fig1\" class=\"link xref-fig\">1</a>, we show the HSC multiband imaging cutouts as well as the PSF-subtracted images, revealing the lens galaxies. In general, the lenses are brighter in <em>y</em> band and the quasars in <em>g</em> band, as expected from their red and blue colours, respectively. We show an additional image of J1002 from data archive of the <em>Hubble Space Telescope</em> (<em>HST</em>) Advanced Camera for Surveys (ACS) Wide Field Channel (WFC), part of the Cosmic Evolution Survey (COSMOS; Koekemoer et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib31\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib31\" data-open=\"bib31\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2007</a>; Scoville et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib49\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib49\" data-open=\"bib49\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2007a</a>,<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib50\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib50\" data-open=\"bib50\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">b</a>) with 5\u03c3 detection limits for point sources of 27.2 AB magnitude in <em>F</em>814<em>W</em>, hereafter COSMOS ACS.</p>                    <a id=\"227346048\" scrollto-destination=\"227346048\"></a>\r\n<div data-id=\"fig1\" data-content-id=\"fig1\" class=\"fig fig-section js-fig-section\" swap-content-for-modal=\"true\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 1.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/502/1/10.1093_mnras_stab145/1/m_stab145fig1.jpeg?Expires=1673672302&amp;Signature=GhI3MKFAQwERrXK2MFI953UFZMHy6Vx4U9yok02hTzJH7y4qURLm6FW-8nzsfwTFEH9KhbfLWlxUuW8GGBSOsX8voDHQh8~41Dezo6Es7ojD5ExKxWe9YoHHBTF3hTSt1j8iB0ulBger-TqHaYXOnK84ezlQr9sE3A0hUOd5cg6v2vPvg7TZIIJEwuWi8TYGihiwCacX-VRM1CLSf4-sqUuTmTKrEg6wyF5JjYEWXSMUbHhNFQ9bSNYY8VRaa~IYZ~DcOzJNlXNF-czARixqnRWluINnC8N8NKEOW-FPVG2yc51H2IdQXwvkA4gqufEAQCI4Mse58jkbo1fjdl0cJQ__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"HSC gri composite and multiband images of the three lensed quasars. Corresponding point source-substracted images based on the <span class=\"small-caps\">galfit</span> best fit in each band are shown below the data. Scale bars of 1 arcsec are displayed in the bottom left corner.</p></div></div>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=227346049 id=\"227346049\" class=\"section-title js-splitscreen-section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec4>4 SPECTROSCOPIC CONFIRMATION</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">Here, we describe our follow-up spectroscopic results for each lens system. All observations were processed using standard techniques within <span class=\"small-caps\">iraf</span>, and flux-calibrated using observations of spectrophotometric standards.</p>                    <h3 scrollto-destination=227346051 id=\"227346051\" class=\"section-title js-splitscreen-section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec4-1>4.1 J0918</h3>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">J0918 system was first discovered by Sonnenfeld et\u00a0al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib55\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib55\" data-open=\"bib55\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2020</a>) as part of the citizen science project <span class=\"small-caps\">spacewarps</span> (Marshall et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib35\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib35\" data-open=\"bib35\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2016</a>; More et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib37\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib37\" data-open=\"bib37\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2016</a>) using over 442\u00a0deg<sup>2</sup> of data from the HSC survey. An expert volunteer, Claude Cornen, identified two blue point-like feature and a putative galaxy in between. A spectrum was obtained with the Inamori Magellan Areal Camera and Spectrograph (IMACS; Dressler et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib14\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib14\" data-open=\"bib14\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2011</a>) on the Baade 6.5-m telescope on 2019 April 1 and 2 (Director\u2019s Discretionary Time, PI: P. Schechter) for a total exposure time 2\u00a0\u00d7\u00a01800\u00a0s using <em>f</em>/2 camera, 0.9 arcsec wide-slit, and 200\u00a0mm<sup>\u22121</sup> grism.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">The 1D spectra of the two point sources correspond to a nearly identical quasar spectrum at <em>z</em><sub>s</sub>\u00a0= 0.804\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.001, based on Mg\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>, O\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>, He\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">i</span>, H\u2009\u03b4, H\u2009\u03b3, H\u2009\u03b2, and O\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span> lines. The blended absorption lines of the lens galaxy with the fainter quasar B can be seen clearly based on Ca K, Ca H, H\u2009\u03b2, Mg b, and Na D, yielding a lens galaxy redshift of <em>z</em><sub>\u2113</sub>\u00a0= 0.459 (see panel a in Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" data-modal-source-id=\"fig2\" class=\"link xref-fig\">2</a>). Together with the presence of a red galaxy in HSC images, the spectra confirm J0918 as a strongly lensed quasar, with image separation 2.26 arcsec.</p>                    <a id=\"227346054\" scrollto-destination=\"227346054\"></a>\r\n<div data-id=\"fig2\" data-content-id=\"fig2\" class=\"fig fig-section js-fig-section\" swap-content-for-modal=\"true\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 2.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/502/1/10.1093_mnras_stab145/1/m_stab145fig2.jpeg?Expires=1673672302&amp;Signature=Vjbo2nGCxwkyYCLNT2kcup7~8970xUaIDzIcePbtFejCfxXZvI8B-9SmofAqoK9dD4WLqqwkv22blaFl7Y8M1qOz0PV2o2AAIxfniWN3O58kjJUlNI2VuJ~f3HQ~ZcP9ohCr9jh5g6rYPJ50ZsFQnESyKLAeSIFZFTiRQ8hj13UTF29Klu49CYXFoJot0VevB1MroEPKRK-J0M8PJxdpEd43SU6xRXyOkk4KD-3hHo-7jkUAFjdSUvnLN4sU4Vx1uv-gHc674wUOmbrIE-MaeDKM6bAhrmClIHLP6aQmSCxMiKTk7MubYhwwlI7clIIt7ojCUmvfjC9Zpl9byDR4Lg__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"1D spectra of J0918 (panel a), J1002 (panels c and d), and J1359 (panel b). Panel (b) shows only the \u2018red part\u2019 of the LRIS spectra, with range 5500\u20138500\u2009\u00c5. The blue and red lines show the two components, demonstrating that they are a nearly identical quasar spectrum, and the grey line in panel (c) is the lens galaxy spectra. Emission and absorption lines are marked by black and grey dashed vertical lines, respectively.\" data-path-from-xml=\"stab145fig2.jpg\" /><div class=\"fig-orig original-slide\"><a class=\"fig-view-orig js-view-large openInAnotherWindow\" href=\"/view-large/figure/227346054/stab145fig2.jpg\" data-path-from-xml=\"stab145fig2.jpg\" target=\"_blank\">Open in new tab</a><a data-section=\"227346054\" href=\"/DownloadFile/DownloadImage.aspx?image=https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/502/1/10.1093_mnras_stab145/1/stab145fig2.jpeg?Expires=1673672302&Signature=fXcSjoOjGOGfP9kUL1lmS3ig-1lFzEXknh0x~6SgbsLuKto3wfTiUlH0kJixBVEJmYZ6ddpruwEe~Tteek5dcYBFJktKa~tAOEnVJHBpKQ~kvyNG0fi-ZfuPdp3Y2TbnjP~ECD3nXdiSsOCv70HUs7yN0COMbY-NEfMjveElEvTQFAfsZFySWn5UJACa0NsM5aU2nI5kcVKRkJQJk40NPAWf71a84ltHvR-hrkkmZIrz6Ujojt6IodrWAeqZcGB~ccaRAtnSatOtHQy4moDCjDtoufQ9HLoUDMGSuvu603uBEOL0GtVr6zquOEhpzx8gJPPxdM8rrExCPQ76t~8Oow__&Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA&sec=227346054&ar=6105347&xsltPath=~/UI/app/XSLT&imagename=&siteId=5326\" class=\"download-slide\" data-path-from-xml=\"stab145fig2.jpg\">Download slide</a></div></div><div class=\"caption fig-caption\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">1D spectra of J0918 (panel a), J1002 (panels c and d), and J1359 (panel b). Panel (b) shows only the \u2018red part\u2019 of the LRIS spectra, with range 5500\u20138500\u2009\u00c5. The blue and red lines show the two components, demonstrating that they are a nearly identical quasar spectrum, and the grey line in panel (c) is the lens galaxy spectra. Emission and absorption lines are marked by black and grey dashed vertical lines, respectively.</p></div></div>                    <h3 scrollto-destination=227346055 id=\"227346055\" class=\"section-title js-splitscreen-section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec4-2>4.2 J1002</h3>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">This candidate was chosen from the <em>Chandra</em> catalogue of X-ray selected objects (Evans et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib15\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib15\" data-open=\"bib15\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2010</a>). These X-ray selected AGN sources were inspected in the optical imaging search for the presence of any close companions (e.g. Liu et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib34\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib34\" data-open=\"bib34\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2013</a>). This system was first detected in the Sloan Digital Sky Survey (SDSS) as SDSS J100201.51+020329.4 as a quasar with spectroscopic redshift of 2.016. Furthermore, this system also has CFHTLS optical and near-infrared imaging, and the COSMOS-Very Large Array (1.4\u00a0GHz) imaging in the radio shows a detection. However, the spatial resolution and sensitivity of these data are not enough to resolve this system. The HSC images of J1002, however, unambiguously reveal the presence of two sources with image separation \u22480.8 arcsec. This is an excellent example of HSC images being ideal for finding small separation lenses. In the COSMOS ACS <em>F</em>814<em>W</em> imaging, we further detect emission from a third object, which is acting as the lens galaxy (see Figs\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" data-modal-source-id=\"fig1\" class=\"link xref-fig\">1</a> and\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" data-modal-source-id=\"fig3\" class=\"link xref-fig\">3</a>). With <span class=\"small-caps\">galfit</span>, we measure magnitudes of <em>A</em>\u00a0= 18.52, <em>B</em>\u00a0= 22.03, and <em>G</em>\u00a0= 21.38 mag.</p>                    <a id=\"227346057\" scrollto-destination=\"227346057\"></a>\r\n<div data-id=\"fig3\" data-content-id=\"fig3\" class=\"fig fig-section js-fig-section\" swap-content-for-modal=\"true\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 3.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/502/1/10.1093_mnras_stab145/1/m_stab145fig3.jpeg?Expires=1673672302&amp;Signature=OeXcC7mT61righGfsz38Fd~QCn2a4Dty2BJ~d2PZRNeoMrHjXH6X7-QwiYiEOg0sfXi0~u6rlWYkt0pF4cW9q012M8yErfPL85i5drcEAq3VOGS3-~mafd5V3PKdCvXt8zUNu17~agVsDsOdfwmhWIecLPA1NiRsWS6OqfUMox-RwiW46kliiUeX9eicTZr~xrqOcckdY6kuPxc8mMD3-tZk7lWOqrSgu-XaXx0Mzp6-Z2RwYBRIQYWIyo61hK5zWrXr5iGrjWSqQZkYJ1wlkeBr4w-6NWKNqBCQaJjQN5RhvZ8QVCBmxAkKzd7Zqzhe27dPIsmg63dDgpeI~E5sbw__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"Panel (a): Model images generated from galfit using a PSF for the source images and a S\u00e9rsic model convolved with the PSF for the lens galaxy, showing the positions of the doubly lensed quasar images (A, B) and the early-type lens galaxy (G) for each system (from top to bottom, J0918, J1002, and J1359, respectively). The black solid bar at the bottom left of the panel shows a scale of 1 arcsec. Panel (b): galfit model-subtracted residual images. Panel (c): Model images generated from lens mass modelling of the lens system, where the source is assumed to be a point source. Magenta and cyan lines indicate critical curves and caustic, respectively. The true source positions are shown by cyan dots. Panel (d): The residual image obtained by subtracting the model from the data.\" data-path-from-xml=\"stab145fig3.jpg\" /><div class=\"fig-orig original-slide\"><a class=\"fig-view-orig js-view-large openInAnotherWindow\" href=\"/view-large/figure/227346057/stab145fig3.jpg\" data-path-from-xml=\"stab145fig3.jpg\" target=\"_blank\">Open in new tab</a><a data-section=\"227346057\" href=\"/DownloadFile/DownloadImage.aspx?image=https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/502/1/10.1093_mnras_stab145/1/stab145fig3.jpeg?Expires=1673672302&Signature=cYg7ObPRhZ52nDssbCUGWGVLB8yzuHViqdPw97CF~g4dsPpfsYpiPxUtsQcgLE8wV~INwcAZOucHd4jAC2gU~RvYpzgNk4NzZCBNmksn8pyrA4AQOEEaW9zO1fidjuNVw2ARKaisx--32gxayqe6U0MlOyqUjYQr16B1E6QAv7jHRYnHeqGWmbAbfBCKbrSRa66DSrVKXMob1l17TI0yFr5AE9mQvdQO52S0KpDAHmu7aUQ9KCvjpLXn0mTz8x4heRYknnSywn1eoLt16nL4CnRyGZpfwpCru-T5~fBPuEvgB7MZUA5Fvp8FD4Z5JM0tYFgzHfi34ioWJAV6vdtzAw__&Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA&sec=227346057&ar=6105347&xsltPath=~/UI/app/XSLT&imagename=&siteId=5326\" class=\"download-slide\" data-path-from-xml=\"stab145fig3.jpg\">Download slide</a></div></div><div class=\"caption fig-caption\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">Panel (a): Model images generated from <span class=\"small-caps\">galfit</span> using a PSF for the source images and a S\u00e9rsic model convolved with the PSF for the lens galaxy, showing the positions of the doubly lensed quasar images (A, B) and the early-type lens galaxy (G) for each system (from top to bottom, J0918, J1002, and J1359, respectively). The black solid bar at the bottom left of the panel shows a scale of 1 arcsec. Panel (b): <span class=\"small-caps\">galfit</span> model-subtracted residual images. Panel (c): Model images generated from lens mass modelling of the lens system, where the source is assumed to be a point source. Magenta and cyan lines indicate critical curves and caustic, respectively. The true source positions are shown by cyan dots. Panel (d): The residual image obtained by subtracting the model from the data.</p></div></div><p class=\"chapter-para\">A near-infrared <em>K</em>-band (22\u2009000\u2009\u00c5) spectrum was obtained with the Infrared Camera and Spectrograph (IRCS; Tokunaga et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib58\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib58\" data-open=\"bib58\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">1998</a>; Kobayashi et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib30\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib30\" data-open=\"bib30\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2000</a>) at Subaru Telescope for a total exposure time 10\u00a0\u00d7\u00a0300\u00a0s using a setup of 0.45\u00a0\u00d7\u00a018.0 arcsec slit, 52 miliarcsec mode, <em>R</em>\u00a0\u223c 400, and <em>K</em>-grism that covers the 19\u2009300\u201324\u2009800\u2009\u00c5\u00a0 range, assisted with the Adaptive Optics system AO188 (Hayano et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib20\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib20\" data-open=\"bib20\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2008</a>, <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib21\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib21\" data-open=\"bib21\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2010</a>), on 2012 November 27 (o12438, PI: M. Schramm). The 1D spectra of the two sources show the same broad emission line of H\u2009\u03b1 at <em>z</em><sub>s</sub>\u00a0= 2.016\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.003. The results suggest that the fainter quasar is highly likely to be at the same redshift as the brighter quasar (see panel d of Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" data-modal-source-id=\"fig2\" class=\"link xref-fig\">2</a>).</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">We also carried out deep optical spectroscopy to obtain the redshift of the lens galaxy. We used the Faint Object Camera and Spectrograph (FOCAS; Kashikawa et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib28\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib28\" data-open=\"bib28\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2002</a>) at Subaru Telescope on 2014 October 23 (o14500, PI: A. More). The observations were made with 1 arcsec long-slit mode, a 300R grating, and an SO58 order-cut filter, giving a spectral coverage of 5800\u201310\u2009000\u2009\u00c5\u00a0 with a dispersion of 1.34\u2009\u00c5\u00a0pixel<sup>\u22121</sup> for a total exposure time 3\u00a0\u00d7\u00a0900\u00a0s. We detect absorption lines from the lens galaxy based on Ca K, Ca H, <em>G</em> band, H \u03b2, Mg b, and Na D at <em>z</em><sub>\u2113</sub>\u00a0= 0.439\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.001 (see panel c of Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" data-modal-source-id=\"fig2\" class=\"link xref-fig\">2</a>).</p>                    <h3 scrollto-destination=227346060 id=\"227346060\" class=\"section-title js-splitscreen-section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec4-3>4.3 J1359</h3>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">J1359 system was listed as a likely lens candidate by the Sloan Digital Sky Survey Quasar Lens Search (SQLS; e.g. Oguri et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib40\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib40\" data-open=\"bib40\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2006</a>; Inada et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib22\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib22\" data-open=\"bib22\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2012</a>), however follow-up observations had not been performed due to the small separation (\u22641 arcsec). We reinspected the SQLS candidate lists using HSC images and re-graded this system as a highly likely candidate. We can clearly observe an extended object (galaxy) between two point sources with quite similar colours (see Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" data-modal-source-id=\"fig1\" class=\"link xref-fig\">1</a>). The quasar was first detected in the SDSS as SDSS J135944.21+012809.8 and has a spectroscopic redshift of 1.096. This system was including as a part of program to confirm dual quasars i.e. physical pairs (Silverman et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib51\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib51\" data-open=\"bib51\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2020</a>).</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">We performed spectroscopic follow-up using the dual beam Low Resolution Imaging Spectrometer (LRIS; Oke et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib43\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib43\" data-open=\"bib43\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">1995</a>; Steidel et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib56\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib56\" data-open=\"bib56\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2004</a>) at the Keck 1 telescope on 2019 January 10 as a backup target during the COSMOS Ly\u2009\u03b1 Mapping And Tomography Observations (CLAMATO) Survey (Lee et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib33\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib33\" data-open=\"bib33\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2018</a>; U095, PI White). We exposed for 600\u2009s in the blue and 590\u2009s in the red using the 1 arcsec width long-slit, the 5600\u2009\u00c5\u00a0 dichroic, the 600 \u2113 mm<sup>\u22121</sup> blue grism (\u03bb<sub>blaze</sub>\u00a0= 4000\u2009\u00c5), and the 400 \u2113 mm<sup>\u22121</sup> red grating (\u03bb<sub>blaze</sub>\u00a0= 8500\u2009\u00c5). In panel (b) of Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" data-modal-source-id=\"fig2\" class=\"link xref-fig\">2</a>, we can see separated spectra of the brighter and the fainter quasar, both at <em>z</em><sub>s</sub>\u00a0= 1.096\u00a0\u00b1\u00a00.001 from the identification of several emission lines, Mg\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>, Ne\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">v</span>, Ne\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">vi</span>, O\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>, He\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">i</span>, S\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>, and H\u0394, in the red spectra. Unfortunately, we cannot extract the lens galaxy information in the blue spectra due to bad seeing. We find a tentative hint of the 4000\u2009\u00c5\u00a0 break feature, which corresponds to redshift <em>z</em><sub>\u2113</sub>\u00a0\u2248 0.35. This is also consistent with our rough estimation of the lens redshift, based on the HSC colours.</p>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=227346063 id=\"227346063\" class=\"section-title js-splitscreen-section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec5>5 LENSING PROPERTIES</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">We used the publicly available lens modelling software <span class=\"small-caps\">glafic</span> (Oguri <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib38\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib38\" data-open=\"bib38\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2010</a>) to model the lensing configuration of the three systems. In order to explore the parameter posteriors, we ran a custom code that combines <span class=\"small-caps\">glafic</span> and the <span class=\"small-caps\">emcee</span> (Foreman-Mackey et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib18\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib18\" data-open=\"bib18\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2013</a>) to perform Markov Chain Monte Carlo (MCMC) sampling. With the exception of J1002, where we fitted the COSMOS data, we used the flux information in image pixels (within 7.56, 2.25, and 5.88 arcsec of J0918, J1002, and J1359, respectively) of the lens galaxies and the quasar images in the HSC <em>i</em> band image, which has better seeing, as constraints for the lens mass model.</p><div class=\"&#xA;            block-child-p&#xA;            \">Light from the lens galaxy and the unresolved source quasars is modelled with a seven-parameter elliptical S\u00e9rsic profile and a three-parameter PSF profile, respectively. We used the best-fitting parameters from <span class=\"small-caps\">galfit</span> with prior knowledge of the position, the ellipticity, and position angle from <em>i</em> band as initial parameters input to <span class=\"small-caps\">galfic</span> to model the lens galaxy G. For the source, we let every parameter of the PSF profile vary: magnitude and as well as positions <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\rm \\mathit{ x}_{s}$|\u2060</span>, <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\rm \\mathit{ y}_{s}$|\u2060</span>. We consider a singular isothermal ellipsoid (SIE), with surface density given by <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$\\kappa =\\theta _{\\rm Ein}/(2\\sqrt{\\tilde{x}^2+\\tilde{y}^2/(1-e)^2})$|</span> where <span class=\"inline-formula no-formula-id\">|$(\\tilde{x}, \\tilde{y})$|</span> are the coordinates relative to the lens centre along the semimajor and semiminor axes of the elliptical mass distribution, for the lens mass model. The mass distribution is optimized in the image plane by minimizing \u03c7<sup>2</sup> the flux information between the observed and lens model image. The inferred angular Einstein radius and enclosed mass is defined by <div class=\"formula-wrap\"><div class=\"disp-formula\" id=\"equ1\" content-id=\"equ1\"><div class=\"tex-math display-math\">$$\\begin{eqnarray*}\r\n\\theta _{\\rm Ein}=4\\pi \\left(\\frac{\\sigma _{\\rm SIE}}{c}\\right)^2\\frac{D_{\\rm \\ell s}}{D_{\\rm s}}\r\n\\end{eqnarray*}$$</div></div><span class=\"label\">(1)</span></div>and <div class=\"formula-wrap\"><div class=\"disp-formula\" id=\"equ2\" content-id=\"equ2\"><div class=\"tex-math display-math\">$$\\begin{eqnarray*}\r\nM_{\\rm Ein}=\\pi \\Sigma _{\\rm cr}(\\theta _{\\rm Ein}D_{\\ell })^2\r\n\\end{eqnarray*}$$</div></div><span class=\"label\">(2)</span></div>with \u03a3<sub>cr</sub>\u00a0= <em>c</em><sup>2</sup><em>D</em><sub>s</sub>/(4\u03c0<em>GD</em><sub>\u2113</sub><em>D</em><sub>\u2113s</sub>) in terms of angular diameter distance to the source <em>D</em><sub>s</sub>, to the lens <em>D</em><sub>\u2113</sub>, between the observer and the source <em>D</em><sub>\u2113s</sub>, with gravitational constant <em>G</em>, and the speed of light <em>c</em>. The results of lens modelling are summarized in Table\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-tbl2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"tbl2\" data-open=\"tbl2\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">2</a> and Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" data-modal-source-id=\"fig3\" class=\"link xref-fig\">3</a> for <em>i</em> band. Note for J1359 we used an estimated lens redshift <em>z</em><sub>\u2113</sub>\u00a0= 0.35 for the lens mass model.</div>                    <a id=\"227346066\" scrollto-destination=\"227346066\"></a>\r\n<div content-id=\"tbl2\" class=\"table-modal table-full-width-wrap\"><div class=\"table-wrap table-wide\"><div class=\"table-wrap-title\" id=\"tbl2\" class=\"&#xA;          graphic-wrap&#xA;          \"><a class=\"fig-view-orig openInAnotherWindow btn js-view-large\" target=\"_blank\" href=\"/view-large/227346066\">\r\n          Open in new tab\r\n        </a></div></div></div>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=227346067 id=\"227346067\" class=\"section-title js-splitscreen-section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec6>6 CONCLUSIONS</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">We have presented the spectroscopic confirmation of three new doubly lensed quasars, compiled from distinct catalogues. The HSC images of J0918 and J1359 reveal two quasar images on either side of lensing source, separated by 2.26 and 1.05 arcsec, respectively, and a close companion for J1002. COSMOS ACS image shows two resolved quasar images and a putative lens galaxy for J1002. Spectra confirm that each system is a lensing system with <em>z</em><sub>s</sub>\u00a0= 0.804, 2.016, and <em>z</em><sub>\u2113</sub>\u00a0= 0.459, 0.439, for J0918 and J1002, respectively. J1359 has two quasar spectra at <em>z</em><sub>s</sub>\u00a0= 1.096 with similar features and the lens spectrum cannot be extracted due to poor seeing during observation.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">We fit SIE lens models to the lenses and infer the Einstein radius and enclosed mass. J1002 and J1359 have velocity dispersion \u03c3<sub>SIE</sub>\u00a0= 155 and 172\u00a0km s<sup>\u22121</sup> corresponding to enclosed mass within \u03b8<sub>Ein</sub> of <em>M</em><sub>Ein</sub>\u00a0= 0.62\u00a0\u00d7\u00a010<sup>11</sup> and 0.74\u00a0\u00d7\u00a010<sup>11</sup> \u00a0<em>h</em><sup>\u22121</sup>M<sub>\u2299</sub>, respectively. Hence, these systems provide the opportunity to study galaxies from the lower end of the mass function compared to the typical galaxies that have been studied with gravitational lensing so far.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">The discovery of these lenses shows us the importance of reanalysis or re-inspection of previous lens search catalogues, by comparing to ongoing or upcoming imaging surveys of superior quality. We have shown that the unique combination of deep, wide imaging, high pixel resolution and good seeing conditions of the HSC data make possible to discover small separation lenses as part of the ongoing SuGOHI search.</p>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=227346071 id=\"227346071\" class=\"backacknowledgements-title js-splitscreen-backacknowledgements-title\" data-legacy-id=ack1>ACKNOWLEDGEMENTS</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">This work was supported by JSPS KAKENHI Grant Number JP17H02868 (ATJ, KTI), JP15H05892, JP18K03693 (MO), JP15H05896,JP20K04016 (IK), and JP18H05868 (KGL). G.</div></span> \u00a0et al.\u00a0</span>, <div class=\"year\">2000</div>, <div class=\"source \">AJ</div>, <div class=\"volume\">120</div>, <div class=\"fpage\">1579</div> \u00a0<div class=\"pub-id\"><a href=\"https://doi.org/10.1086/301513\" class=\"link link-doi openInAnotherWindow\" target=\"_blank\">10.1086/301513</a></div></p><!--citationLinks: case 1--><div class=\"citation-links\"></div><div class=\"citation-links\"><div class=\"crossref-doi js-ref-link\"><a class=\"openInAnotherWindow\" href=\"http://dx.doi.org/10.1086/301513\" target=\"_blank\">Crossref</a></div><div class=\"adsDoiReference\"><a class=\"openInAnotherWindow\" href=\"http://adsabs.harvard.edu/cgi-bin/basic_connect?qsearch=10.1086%2F301513\" target=\"_blank\">Search ADS</a></div><div class=\"xslopenurl empty-target\"><span class=\"inst-open-url-holders\" data-targetId=\"10.1086%2F301513\"> </span></div>\u00a0</div></div></div></div></div></div>                    <h3 scrollto-destination=227346084 id=\"227346084\" class=\"appendix-title js-splitscreen-appendix-title\" data-legacy-id=sec7>APPENDIX A: REJECTED CANDIDATES</h3>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">By using the same instrument setup for observing J0918 spectra, we observed two other candidates HSC J113957.93\u2212001010.8 and HSC J120755.44\u2212010438.5, for a total exposure time 1800\u00a0s per system (see Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-figa1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" data-modal-source-id=\"figa1\" class=\"link xref-fig\">A1</a>), which we convincingly reject. The first candidate was made up of four blue components in a quad-like configuration, with odd flux ratios. The close pair should have been brighter and the quadrilateral made by the four images has two opposite sides that are twice as big as the other pair of opposite sides. The spectrum of the two brightest components showed ionized knots with H\u2009\u03b2, O\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>, and H\u2009\u03b1 which indicate a bunch of star-forming regions likely associated with a galaxy at <em>z</em>\u00a0\u223c 0.05. The spectrum of second candidate likewise showed narrow H\u2009\u03b2 and O\u2009<span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span> at <em>z</em>\u00a0= 0.37.</p>                    <a id=\"227346086\" scrollto-destination=\"227346086\"></a>\r\n<div data-id=\"figa1\" data-content-id=\"figa1\" class=\"fig fig-section js-fig-section\" swap-content-for-modal=\"true\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure A1.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/502/1/10.1093_mnras_stab145/1/m_stab145figa1.jpeg?Expires=1673672302&amp;Signature=SA5m-zYJjg0PvBod1N2vE7atxNo67Sz5czpQgq2DQy5sxUV7lpXCMcHhNB2pMluk2npUE4vQHjpIAHluHQPswyWez41N8NcFD~hdQK7UTTN2VA9yBacm48LjZ54vwcpMtyFxaGFBDoIMtg5dfSpidWOhPrv30xDYQ86RtkRETDHg~7-Q759gkqGeLd62Aa2vopL7VC1RwVfpLCRXVMIQLdMe0pJoD18cn4Oy~aQg-CFHtR3msUC4GHqNVQVR2gy~HAeutRBUhiAbzvVS7DCYcMkmG8hEzixrM0HDDzctCY3XvEk6jdSnlUPt0o378mazolxU3ms~OK4ax5fhbFxILQ__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"HSC gri composite images of the the two rejected candidates. widget-instance-OUP_Article_FullText_Widget\">\n        <div class=\"module-widget\">\r\n    <div class=\"widget-items\" data-widgetname=\"ArticleFulltext\">\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n                    <h2 scrollto-destination=227346033 id=\"227346033\" class=\"abstract-title js-splitscreen-abstract-title\" >ABSTRACT</h2>\r\n<section class=\"abstract\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">We present spectroscopic confirmation of three new two-image gravitationally lensed quasars, compiled from existing strong lens and X-ray catalogues. Images of HSC J091843.27\u2013022007.5 show a red galaxy with two blue point sources at either side, separated by 2.26 arcsec. This system has a source and a lens redshifts <em>z</em><sub>s</sub>\u00a0= 0.804 and <em>z</em><sub>\u2113</sub>\u00a0= 0.459, respectively, as obtained by our follow-up spectroscopic data. CXCO J100201.50+020330.0 shows two point sources separated by 0.85 arcsec on either side of an early-type galaxy. The follow-up spectroscopic data confirm the fainter quasar has the same redshift with the brighter quasar from the Sloan Digital Sky Survey (SDSS) fiber spectrum at <em>z</em><sub>s</sub>\u00a0= 2.016. The deflecting foreground galaxy is a typical early-type galaxy at a redshift of <em>z</em><sub>\u2113</sub>\u00a0= 0.439. SDSS J135944.21+012809.8 has two point sources with quasar spectra at the same redshift <em>z</em><sub>s</sub>\u00a0= 1.096, separated by 1.05 arcsec, and fits to the HSC images confirm the presence of a galaxy between these. These discoveries demonstrate the power of the Hyper Suprime-Cam Subaru Strategic Program (HSC-SSP)\u2019s deep imaging and wide sky coverage. Combined with existing X-ray source catalogues and follow-up spectroscopy, the HSC-SSP provides us unique opportunities to find multiple-image quasars lensed by a foreground galaxy.</p></section>                    <div class=\"article-metadata-panel clearfix at-ArticleMetadata\"></div>\r\n<div class=\"kwd-group\"><a class=\"kwd-part kwd-main\" href=\"javascript:;\" data-keyword=\"&quot;gravitational lensing: strong&quot;\">gravitational lensing: strong</a>, <a class=\"kwd-part kwd-main\" href=\"javascript:;\" data-keyword=\"&quot;methods: observational&quot;\">methods: observational</a></div>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=227346035 id=\"227346035\" class=\"section-title js-splitscreen-section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec1>1 INTRODUCTION</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">Over the four decades since the discovery of the first gravitationally lensed quasar (Walsh, Carswell &amp; Weymann <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib62\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib62\" data-open=\"bib62\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">1979</a>), these systems have proven to be invaluable probes for both astrophysics and cosmology (e.g. Claeskens &amp; Surdej <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib10\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib10\" data-open=\"bib10\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2002</a>; Treu &amp; Marshall <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib59\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib59\" data-open=\"bib59\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2016</a>). Astrophysical applications range from intermediate redshifts, with the measurement of extragalactic extinction curves (e.g. Falco et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib16\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib16\" data-open=\"bib16\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">1999</a>; \u00d8stman, Goobar &amp; M\u00f6rtsell <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib67\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib67\" data-open=\"bib67\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2008</a>), the direct detection of dark matter substructures (e.g. Dalal &amp; Kochanek <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib11\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib11\" data-open=\"bib11\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2002</a>; Vegetti et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib60\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib60\" data-open=\"bib60\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2012</a>), constraints on Warm Dark Matter (WDM; e.g. Inoue et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib23\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib23\" data-open=\"bib23\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>), microlensing studies Vernardos &amp; Tsagkatakis (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib61\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib61\" data-open=\"bib61\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2019</a>), and the calibration of the stellar mass Fundamental Plane (e.g. Schechter et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib48\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib48\" data-open=\"bib48\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2014</a>), to high redshifts, with elucidating the structure of quasar accretion discs (e.g. Yonehara et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib65\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib65\" data-open=\"bib65\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">1998</a>; Poindexter, Morgan &amp; Kochanek <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib46\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib46\" data-open=\"bib46\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2008</a>), their broad line regions (e.g. Sluse et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib52\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib52\" data-open=\"bib52\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2012</a>; Fian et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib17\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib17\" data-open=\"bib17\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2018</a>), and the coevolution of supermassive black holes with their hosts galaxies (e.g. Peng et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib45\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib45\" data-open=\"bib45\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2006</a>; Ding et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib13\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib13\" data-open=\"bib13\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>). In cosmology, statistically complete samples of lensed quasars are used to set constraints on dark energy (e.g. Oguri et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib41\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib41\" data-open=\"bib41\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2008</a>, <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib42\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib42\" data-open=\"bib42\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2012</a>), and lensed quasars with measured time delays are used to infer the Hubble\u2013Lema\u00eetre constant independent from other probes (e.g. Suyu et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib57\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib57\" data-open=\"bib57\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2010</a>; Bonvin et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib7\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib7\" data-open=\"bib7\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>; Wong et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib64\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib64\" data-open=\"bib64\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2019</a>).</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">While these applications are broad, they all require distinct sample selection criteria, such that studies utilizing lensed quasars are limited at present by the small number of \u223c220 known systems.<sup><span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fn1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fn1\" data-open=\"fn1\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-fn js-xref-fn\">1</a></sup> None the less, the numbers have increased considerably over the past decade and a half, due to the availability of large-scale, deep multiband optical imaging surveys such as the Sloan Digital Sky Survey (SDSS; York et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib66\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib66\" data-open=\"bib66\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2000</a>), and more recently the Panoramic Survey Telescope and Rapid Response System (Pan-STARRS; Chambers et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib8\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib8\" data-open=\"bib8\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2016</a>), the Dark Energy Survey (DES; Abbott et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib1\" data-open=\"bib1\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2018</a>), the Hyper Suprime-Cam Subaru Strategic Program (HSC-SSP; Aihara et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib3\" data-open=\"bib3\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2018a</a>), and the Dark Energy Spectroscopic Instrument (DESI) Legacy Imaging Surveys (Dey et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib12\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib12\" data-open=\"bib12\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2019</a>). Various data mining techniques have been employed to isolate the intrinsically rare lensed quasars (Oguri &amp; Marshall <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib39\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib39\" data-open=\"bib39\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2010</a>) among the vast amounts of possible contaminants. These include selecting from a parent spectroscopic catalogue and applying morphological and colour criteria (e.g. Oguri et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib40\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib40\" data-open=\"bib40\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2006</a>), using machine learning techniques on both catalogue and pixel data (e.g. Agnello et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib2\" data-open=\"bib2\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>), or engaging citizen science volunteers to visually inspect large numbers of images (e.g. Sonnenfeld et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib55\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib55\" data-open=\"bib55\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2020</a>). Ultimately however, to convincingly confirm a system as a lensed quasar requires extensive follow-up spectroscopy campaigns, which is why publishing lists of candidates is common in the literature (e.g. Rusu et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib47\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib47\" data-open=\"bib47\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2019</a>; Chan et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib9\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib9\" data-open=\"bib9\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2020</a>).</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">In this paper, we present the spectroscopic confirmation of three new strongly lensed quasars compiled from previous catalogues applied to the HSC-SSP footprint: HSC J091843.27\u2013022007.5, CXCO J100201.50+020330.0, and SDSS J135944.21+012809.8 (hereafter J0918, J1002, and J1359) at (RA, Dec.) = (139.6803, \u22122.3354), (150.5063, +2.0582), and (209.9342, +1.4693), respectively. Our paper is organized as follows. Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec2\"></span><a href=\"#sec2\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec js-xref-sec\">2</a> briefly illustrates the candidate-compilation process. In Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec3\"></span><a href=\"#sec3\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec js-xref-sec\">3</a>, we describe the imaging analysis. We present the results of the spectroscopic follow-up observations of the systems in Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec4\"></span><a href=\"#sec4\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec js-xref-sec\">4</a>. In Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec5\"></span><a href=\"#sec5\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec js-xref-sec\">5</a>, we present the mass modelling of the systems, and we conclude in Section\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec6\"></span><a href=\"#sec6\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec js-xref-sec\">6</a>. Throughout this paper, we adopt a concordance cosmology with \u03a9<sub>m</sub>\u00a0= 0.27, \u03a9<sub>\u039b</sub>\u00a0= 0.73, <em>H</em><sub>0</sub>\u00a0= 73\u00a0km s<sup>\u22121</sup> Mpc<sup>\u22121</sup>. All quoted magnitudes are on the AB system, position angles are measured East of North, and uncertainties are 1\u03c3 and are assumed to be Gaussian.</p>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=227346039 id=\"227346039\" class=\"section-title js-splitscreen-section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec2>2 LENSED QUASAR CANDIDATE COMPILATION</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">The lens candidates we report here are not the result of a single systematic search. Instead, we compiled candidates from three different methods employed by several of the authors: looking for close companion object in the Chandra catalogue of X-ray selected objects (Evans et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib15\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib15\" data-open=\"bib15\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2010</a>), carried out by co-author Anupreeta More, re-inspection of the Sloan Digital Sky Survey Quasar Lens Search (SQLS; e.g. Oguri et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib40\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib40\" data-open=\"bib40\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2006</a>; Inada et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib22\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib22\" data-open=\"bib22\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2012</a>) catalogue, conducted by co-author Issha Kayo, and further examination of the Survey of Gravitationally lensed Objects in HSC Imaging (SuGOHI; Sonnenfeld et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib53\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib53\" data-open=\"bib53\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2018</a>, <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib54\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib54\" data-open=\"bib54\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2019</a>, <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib55\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib55\" data-open=\"bib55\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2020</a>; Wong et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib63\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib63\" data-open=\"bib63\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2018</a>; Chan et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib9\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib9\" data-open=\"bib9\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2020</a>; Jaelani et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib26\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib26\" data-open=\"bib26\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2020</a>).</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">As preliminary selection, we checked 5 candidates of SQLS on HSC footprint to see whether we can clearly observe an extended object (galaxy) between two point sources with quite similar colours. J1359 was the only promising candidate for spectroscopic follow-up. We selected 3 of 15 candidates from the SuGOHI lenses (e.g. Chan et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib9\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib9\" data-open=\"bib9\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2020</a>; Jaelani et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib26\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib26\" data-open=\"bib26\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2020</a>; Sonnenfeld et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib55\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib55\" data-open=\"bib55\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2020</a>) based on their brightness and with suitable coordinates for follow-up.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">In total, we selected 5 candidates, two from the first two methods each, and three from SuGOHI, for conducting follow-up spectroscopic observations. Details of each candidate are described in the next sections.</p>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=227346043 id=\"227346043\" class=\"section-title js-splitscreen-section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec3>3 IMAGING</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">In this work, we use photometric data from the HSC Wide S18A internal data release of the HSC survey (Aihara et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib5\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib5\" data-open=\"bib5\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2019</a>). The HSC Survey is an ongoing imaging survey, expected to cover about 1400\u00a0deg<sup>2</sup> in five bands (<em>g, r, i, z</em>, and <em>y</em>) down to <em>r</em>\u00a0\u223c 26 with the Hyper Suprime-Cam (Aihara et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib3\" data-open=\"bib3\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2018a</a>; Furusawa et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib19\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib19\" data-open=\"bib19\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2018</a>; Kawanomoto et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib29\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib29\" data-open=\"bib29\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2018</a>; Komiyama et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib32\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib32\" data-open=\"bib32\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2018</a>; Miyazaki et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib36\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib36\" data-open=\"bib36\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2018</a>), using a wide-field (1.7-deg diameter) optical camera installed on the 8.2-m Subaru Telescope. The data are processed with <span class=\"small-caps\">hscpipe</span>, which is derived from the Vera C. Rubin Observatory\u2019s Legacy Survey of Space and Time pipeline (Ivezi\u0107 et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib25\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib25\" data-open=\"bib25\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2008</a>, <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib24\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib24\" data-open=\"bib24\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2019</a>; Axelrod et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib6\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib6\" data-open=\"bib6\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2010</a>; Juri\u0107 et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib27\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib27\" data-open=\"bib27\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2017</a>).</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">We model and analyse the multiband HSC imaging data for the lens systems using <span class=\"small-caps\">galfit</span> (Peng et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib44\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib44\" data-open=\"bib44\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2002</a>). For each system, we measure relative positions of the fainter quasar and the lens galaxy with respect to the brighter quasar, by fitting a model composed of a point source for each quasar image and a S\u00e9rsic profile convolved with the point spread function (PSF) for the lens galaxy. The PSF models are generated using the <span class=\"monospace\">PSF Picker</span> tool Aihara et\u00a0al. (see details in <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib4\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib4\" data-open=\"bib4\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2018b</a>, <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib5\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib5\" data-open=\"bib5\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2019</a>) for all of the HSC bands. Magnitudes of each component, derived from the fits, are given in Table\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-tbl1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"tbl1\" data-open=\"tbl1\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">1</a>.</p>                    <a id=\"227346046\" scrollto-destination=\"227346046\"></a>\r\n<div content-id=\"tbl1\" class=\"table-modal table-full-width-wrap\"><div class=\"table-wrap table-wide\"><div class=\"table-wrap-title\" id=\"tbl1\" data-id=\"tbl1\"><span class=\"label\">Table 1.</span><div class=\"caption\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">Properties of three confirmed lensed quasars. The redshifts of lens and source are obtained from our follow-up spectra. The relative astrometry in <em>i</em> band in arcsec, and the magnitudes of the brighter (A), the fainter (B) quasar image, and the lens galaxy (G) are obtained by fitting the HSC images using <span class=\"small-caps\">galfit</span>. The HSC image quality, in terms of the \u2018seeing\u2019 FWHM in arcsec, is also quoted. A tentative result <em>z</em><sub>\u2113</sub>\u00a0= 0.35 for J1359.</p></div> </div><div class=\"table-overflow\"><table role=\"table\"><thead><tr><th>System [<em>z</em><sub>\u2113</sub>,        </a></div></div></div><p class=\"chapter-para\">In Fig.\u00a0<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" data-modal-source-id=\"fig1\" class=\"link In general, the lenses are brighter in <em>y</em> band and the quasars in <em>g</em> band, as expected from their red and blue colours, respectively. We show an additional image of J1002 from data archive of the <em>Hubble Space Telescope</em> (<em>HST</em>) Advanced Camera for Surveys (ACS) Wide Field Channel (WFC), part of the Cosmic Evolution Survey (COSMOS; Koekemoer et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib31\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib31\" data-open=\"bib31\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2007</a>; Scoville et\u00a0al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib49\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib49\" data-open=\"bib49\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2007a</a>,<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib50\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib50\" data-open=\"bib50\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">b</a>) with 5\u03c3 detection limits for point sources of 27.2 AB magnitude in <em>F</em>814<em>W</em>, hereafter COSMOS ACS.</p>                    <a id=\"227346048\" scrollto-destination=\"227346048\"></a>\r\n<div data-id=\"fig1\" data-content-id=\"fig1\" class=\"fig fig-section js-fig-section\" swap-content-for-modal=\"true\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 1.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/502/1/10.1093_mnras_stab145/1/m_stab145fig1.jpeg?Expires=1673672302&amp;Signature=GhI3MKFAQwERrXK2MFI953UFZMHy6Vx4U9yok02hTzJH7y4qURLm6FW-8nzsfwTFEH9KhbfLWlxUuW8GGBSOsX8voDHQh8~41Dezo6Es7ojD5ExKxWe9YoHHBTF3hTSt1j8iB0ulBger-TqHaYXOnK84ezlQr9sE3A0hUOd5cg6v2vPvg7TZIIJEwuWi8TYGihiwCacX-VRM1CLSf4-sqUuTmTKrEg6wyF5JjYEWXSMUbHhNFQ9bSNYY8VRaa~IYZ~DcOzJNlXNF-czARixqnRWluINnC8N8NKEOW-FPVG2yc51H2IdQXwvkA4gqufEAQCI4Mse58jkbo1fjdl0cJQ__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"HSC gri composite and multiband images of the three lensed quasars.
